It then checks if the string representation of the error is `\"DeserializationError\"`. \n\nHowever, look at the logic:\n- If `str(e) != \"DeserializationError\"`: it RE-RAISES the exception\n- Otherwise (if it equals \"DeserializationError\"): it shows an error message\n\nThis means that if a `ValueError` is thrown that is NOT specifically `\"DeserializationError\"`, it will be re-raised as an unhandled exception, causing a crash.\n\nLooking at the comment on line 218-219: \"All Rust exceptions get turned into a ValueError by python-adblock\" - this suggests that there might be different kinds of deserialization errors that could result in different ValueError messages.\n\n\nThe actual error message from the adblock library probably doesn't match `\"DeserializationError\"` exactly, causing the exception to be re-raised instead of handled gracefully. ValueError). This\ncauses the exception to propagate as unhandled, crashing the application\nduring startup.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport pathlib\nimport tempfile\nimport sys\nfrom unittest import mock\n\npytest = __import__(\"pytest\")\npytest.importorskip(\"adblock\")\n\nimport adblock\n\n\ndef test_corrupted_cache_deserialization_error():\n    \"\"\"Test that corrupted cache files raise DeserializationError, not ValueError.\n\n    This test directly demonstrates the root cause of the bug:\n    - adblock.Engine.deserialize_from_file() raises adblock.DeserializationError\n    - adblock.DeserializationError is NOT a subclass of ValueError\n    - Therefore, braveadblock.read_cache() which catches ValueError will NOT\n      catch the DeserializationError, allowing it to propagate as unhandled\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        cache_path = pathlib.Path(tmpdir) / \"corrupted.dat\"\n        cache_path.write_bytes(b\"corrupted binary data\")\n\n        engine = adblock.Engine(adblock.FilterSet())\n\n        # Verify that the exception is DeserializationError, not ValueError\n        with pytest.raises(adblock.DeserializationError):\n            engine.deserialize_from_file(str(cache_path))\n\n        # Verify that DeserializationError is NOT a ValueError\n        assert not issubclass(adblock.DeserializationError, ValueError)\n\n\ndef test_braveadblock_read_cache_with_corrupted_file():\n    \"\"\"Test that BraveAdBlocker.read_cache() crashes on corrupted cache.\n\n    This is the regression test that demonstrates the actual bug.\n    The read_cache() method only catches ValueError, but the adblock library\n    raises adblock.DeserializationError. Therefore, the `except ValueError` clause does NOT catch it\n4. The exception propagates as unhandled, crashing the application during startup\n5. Check if it's a deserialization error by message or type\n    if \"Deserialization\" in str(type(e).__name__):\n        message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                      \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n    else:\n        raise\n```\n\n## Files Modified\n\n- `/workspace/regression_test.py` - Created comprehensive regression test\n\n## Files Analyzed\n\n- `/app/qutebrowser/components/braveadblock.py` - Bug location\n- `/app/tests/unit/components/test_braveadblock.py` - Existing test suite\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe regression test clearly demonstrates that:\n1. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01VSuBFzTTzaqGgMDvQjE8iw","type":"tool_result","content":"# Ad-Blocker Cache Corruption Bug Investigation\n\n## Summary\n\nI have successfully identified and documented the root cause of the qutebrowser ad-blocker cache corruption crash, and created a comprehensive regression test.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `/app/qutebrowser/components/braveadblock.py`, line 216-220 in the `read_cache()` method\n\n**The Bug:**\n```python\ntry:\n    self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))\nexcept ValueError as e:\n    if str(e) != \"DeserializationError\":\n        raise\n    message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                  \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n```\n\n**Why it's broken:**\n1. When the cache file is corrupted, `adblock.Engine.deserialize_from_file()` raises `adblock.DeserializationError`\n2. `adblock.DeserializationError` is **NOT** a subclass of `ValueError`\n3. Therefore, the `except ValueError` clause does NOT catch it\n4. The exception propagates as unhandled, crashing the application during startup\n5. The user cannot use qutebrowser until they manually delete the cache file\n\n**Proof:**\n```python\n>>> import adblock\n>>> issubclass(adblock.DeserializationError, ValueError)\nFalse\n```\n\n## Expected vs Actual Behavior\n\n**Expected Behavior:**\n- Application handles corrupted cache gracefully\n- Logs an error message\n- Continues running with ad-blocker disabled until cache is rebuilt\n- User can still browse the web\n\n**Actual Behavior:**\n- Application crashes with unhandled `DeserializationError`\n- User cannot use qutebrowser at all\n- Must manually delete cache file: `~/.config/qutebrowser/adblock-cache.dat`\n\n## Regression Test\n\nA comprehensive regression test has been created at `/workspace/regression_test.py` that:\n\n1. **Test 1:** Verifies that corrupted cache files raise `DeserializationError` (not `ValueError`)\n2. **Test 2:** Demonstrates that `BraveAdBlocker.read_cache()` does NOT catch the exception\n3. **Test 3:** Tests empty cache file handling\n4. **Test 4:** Tests random binary data in cache file\n\n### How to Run the Test\n\n```bash\n# Run as a standalone Python script\npython3 /workspace/regression_test.py\n\n# Run with pytest (when environment is properly configured)\npython3 -m pytest -c /dev/null --timeout=60 /workspace/regression_test.py -v\n```\n\n### Test Results\n\nAll 4 tests **PASS**, confirming the bug exists:\n- ✓ DeserializationError is raised (not ValueError)\n- ✓ DeserializationError is NOT a subclass of ValueError  \n- ✓ BraveAdBlocker.read_cache() crashes with corrupted cache\n- ✓ Empty cache files trigger DeserializationError\n\n## Fix (Not Implemented)\n\nThe fix would be to catch `adblock.DeserializationError` instead of `ValueError`, or catch both:\n\n```python\nexcept (ValueError, adblock.DeserializationError) as e:\n    message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                  \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n```\n\nOr more robustly:\n\n```python\nexcept Exception as e:\n    #
